          August Valentine Kautz

          1828-01-05 – 1895-09-04

          Member of Kautz family

          Alternate name(s)

          • August Kautz

          Biographical Information

          August Valentine Kautz was a German-Ammerican officer in the U.S. military who served in the American Civil War. He published two issues of his newspaper Truth Teller in defense of Chief Leschi before Leschi's execution in 1858.

          Spouse(s)

          • Tenas Puss (m. 1853-07)
          • Charlotte Todd Kautz (m. 1865-09-14)
          • Fannie Markbreit Kautz (m. 1872-11-27)

                      Eliza C. Porter

                      Alternate name(s)

                      • Eliza Porter

                      Biographical Information

                      First public school teacher in Chicago, at Fort Dearborn, established normal schools, educated settlers and American Indians at Mackinac Island, aided the wounded during the American Civil War as a member of the U.S. Sanitary Commission, participated in the Underground Railroad, and taught freedmen.

                      Spouse(s)

                      Jeremiah Porter

                              Fannie Markbreit Kautz

                              1849 – 1913-08-11

                              Member of Kautz family

                              Alternate name(s)

                              • Fannie Kautz
                              • Fannie Markbreit
                              • Mrs. Kautz

                              Biographical Information

                              Fannie Markbreit Kautz was a German-American woman who married August Valentine Kautz in 1872. She was known as a socialite talented in dramatics, singing, and painting, and as a charitable woman.

                              August Valentine Kautz

                                    George McClellan

                                    Alternate name(s)

                                    • George B. McClellan

                                    Biographical Information

                                    American soldier, Civil War Union general, civil engineer, railroad executive, and politician who served as the 24th governor of New Jersey.

                                        John Baptist Brondel

                                        Biographical Information

                                        A Belgian-born prelate of the Catholic Church. He served in Canada as Bishop of Vancouver Island (1879–83) and in the United States as Bishop of Helena (1884–1903).

                                        John Ector

                                        Biographical Information

                                        Brother in law of Paymaster Major A.B. Ragan. Ector suffered from some form of mental illness which resulted in violent outbursts and eventually led to his being admitted to an asylum.

                                          Kussass

                                          Member of Snoqualmie Skykomish

                                          Biographical Information

                                          Kussass was a chief of the Skykomish. He was one of six men arrested for the death of Leander Wallace at Fort Nisqually in 1849, and one of two executed.

                                          Newsletter Articles

                                          There are currently no newsletter articles about Kussass.

                                          Biographical Information

                                          Leschi

                                          1808 – 1858-02-19

                                          Member of Nisqually

                                          Biographical Information

                                          War chief of the Nisqually Tribe; accused, tried, and convicted of the murder of two militiamen in a skirmish with his people.

                                            Louis Rossi

                                            Biographical Information

                                            A Catholic missionary priest who ministered for just over three years, from 1856 to 1860 in Washington Territory and then for almost three more years in northern California.

                                            Marcus Whitman

                                            Biographical Information

                                            An American physician and missionary who was killed, along with his wife and 11 other settlers, by a group of Cayuse peoples in an event that came to be known as the Whitman Massacre

                                            Newsletter Articles

                                              Mother Joseph

                                              Biographical Information

                                              A Canadian Religious Sister who led a group of the members of her congregation to the Pacific Northwest of the United States and established a network of schools and healthcare to service the American settlers

                                                    Qualchan

                                                    Died 1858-09-24

                                                    Member of Yakama Klickitat

                                                    Alternate name(s)

                                                    • Qualchin

                                                    Biographical Information

                                                    Qualchan was a Yakama chieftain of the We-ow-icht family. He was a warrior and participated in the Yakama War. He was executed by the U.S. Army in 1858.

                                                    Newsletter Articles

                                                    There are currently no newsletter articles about Qualchan.

                                                    Quallahwowt

                                                    Member of Snoqualmie

                                                    Biographical Information

                                                    Quallahwowt was a sub-chief of the Snoqualmie tribe. He was one of six men arrested for the death of Leander Wallace at Fort Nisqually in 1849, and one of two executed.

                                                    Newsletter Articles

                                                    There are currently no newsletter articles about Quallahwowt.

                                                            Tenas Puss

                                                            1838 – 1891

                                                            Member of Kautz family

                                                            Member of Nisqually

                                                            Alternate name(s)

                                                            • Etta
                                                            • Kitty
                                                            • Kitty Etta Nisqually
                                                            • Kitty Etta Quaymuth
                                                            • Kitty Kautz
                                                            • Little Kitten

                                                            Biographical Information

                                                            Tenas Puss (Little Kitten) was a Nisqually woman who married August Valentine Kautz in the 1850s. She was called Etta or Kitty in English.

                                                                American Fur Company

                                                                Started 1808; ended 1847

                                                                Biographical Information

                                                                The American Fur Company was founded in 1808 by John Jacob Astor to establish a series of fur trading posts at the mouth of the Columbia, at today's Astoria, Oregon.

                                                                Newsletter Articles

                                                                There are currently no newsletter articles about American Fur Company.

                                                                Return to top



                                                                Hudson's Bay Company

                                                                Started 1670-05-02

                                                                Biographical Information

                                                                The Hudson's Bay Company was established by royal charter from King Charles II in 1670.

                                                                Newsletter Articles

                                                                There are currently no newsletter articles about Hudson's Bay Company.

                                                                Return to top



                                                                North West Company

                                                                Started 1779; ended 1821

                                                                Biographical Information

                                                                The North West Company was formed in Montreal in 1779 to directly compete with the Hudson's Bay Company in the fur trade.

                                                                Newsletter Articles

                                                                There are currently no newsletter articles about North West Company.

                                                                    Manifest Destiny

                                                                      American Indian Removal (1830-1847)

                                                                      Newsletter Articles

                                                                      • Newsletter articles about narrower terms
                                                                        Return to top



                                                                        Indian Removal Act of 1830

                                                                        Definition

                                                                        Authorized the president to negotiate with southern Indigenous tribes for their removal to federal territory west of the Mississippi River in exchange for white settlement of their ancestral lands.

                                                                        Newsletter Articles

                                                                        There are currently no newsletter articles about Indian Removal Act of 1830.

                                                                        Return to top



                                                                        Treaty of Medicine Creek (1854)

                                                                        Definition

                                                                        Treaty granted 2.24 million acres of land to the United States in exchange for establishment of three reservations, cash payments over a period of twenty years, and recognition of traditional native fishing and hunting rights.

                                                                        Newsletter Articles

                                                                        There are currently no newsletter articles about Treaty of Medicine Creek (1854).

                                                                        • Newsletter articles about narrower terms
                                                                          Return to top



                                                                          Medicine Creek Treaty Council

                                                                          Newsletter Articles

                                                                          There are currently no newsletter articles about Medicine Creek Treaty Council.

                                                                          Return to top



                                                                          Permanent Indian Frontier (1840)

                                                                          Definition

                                                                          Land reserved through the Indian Removal Act of 1830 which was earmarked for the Native Americans and guaranteed the sovereignty and territorial integrity of the natives and their property.

                                                                          Newsletter Articles

                                                                          There are currently no newsletter articles about Permanent Indian Frontier (1840).

                                                                            Oregon Treaty (1846)

                                                                            Definition

                                                                                                  Puget Sound War (1855-1856)

                                                                                                  Alternate term(s)

                                                                                                  • Indian War (1855-1856)

                                                                                                  Definition

                                                                                                  An armed conflict that took place in the Puget Sound area of the state of Washington in 1855–56, between the United States military, local militias and members of the Indigenous tribes of the Nisqually, Muckleshoot, Puyallup, and Klickitat.

                                                                                                          Catholicism

                                                                                                          Definition

                                                                                                          Core beliefs of Catholicism are found in the Nicene Creed. The Catholic Church teaches that it is the one, holy, catholic and apostolic church founded by Jesus Christ in his Great Commission, that its bishops are the successors of Christ's apostles, and that the pope is the successor to Saint Peter, upon whom primacy was conferred by Jesus Christ.

                                                                                                                                        Historic Fort Steilacoom Association (1983-present)

                                                                                                                                        Definition

                                                                                                                                        Established in 1983, with the purpose of restoring and preserving historic Fort Steilacoom in order to perpetuate the significance of the site for the benefit of the public by operating a museum complex and a strong educational program stressing the role of the Fort in Northwest history.

                                                                                                                                            Fort Steilacoom (1849-1868)

                                                                                                                                            Definition

                                                                                                                                            Founded by the U.S. Army in 1849 near Lake Steilacoom, among the first military fortifications built by the U.S. north of the Columbia River in what was to become the State of Washington, the fort was constructed due to civilian agitation about the massacre in 1847 at the Whitman (Waiilatpu) mission.

                                                                                                                                            Newsletter Articles

                                                                                                                                            There are currently no newsletter articles about Fort Steilacoom (1849-1868).

                                                                                                                                              Oregon Trail

                                                                                                                                              Definition

                                                                                                                                              A 2,170-mile (3,490 km) east–west, large-wheeled wagon route and emigrant trail in the United States that connected the Missouri River to valleys in Oregon.

                                                                                                                                              Newsletter Articles

                                                                                                                                              Oregon Territory (1848-1859)

                                                                                                                                              Definition

                                                                                                                                              Organized incorporated territory of the United States that existed from August 14, 1848, until February 14, 1859, when the southwestern portion of the territory was admitted to the Union as the State of Oregon.

                                                                                                                                                        Waiilatpu Mission

                                                                                                                                                        Definition

                                                                                                                                                        Attempt by two missionary couples, Whitmans and Spaldings, to evangalize indigenous populations of the Pacific Northwest ending with the deaths of the Whitmans and 11 others at the hands of the Cayuse peoples, prompting Congress to declare Oregon a U.S. territory and precipitating the Cayuse war.

                                                                                                                                                              Paiute

                                                                                                                                                              Definition

                                                                                                                                                              Refers to three non-contiguous groups of indigenous peoples of the Great Basin. Although their languages are related within the Numic group of Uto-Aztecan languages, these three groups do not form a single set. The term "Paiute" does not refer to a single, unique, unified group of Great Basin tribes.

                                                                                                                                                              Stikine Tlingit

                                                                                                                                                              Yakama

                                                                                                                                                              • Yakima

                                                                                                                                                              Definition

                                                                                                                                                              Originally occupied the area on both sides of the Columbia River and on the northern branches of the Yakama (formerly Tapteal) and Wenatchee Rivers in the state of Washington. Originally spelled "Yakima," the Yakama nation renamed itself to "Yakama" in the mid-1990s to more closely reflect the proper pronunciation in their native tongue.

                                                                                                                                                                      Whitman Massacre (1847)

                                                                                                                                                                      Definition

                                                                                                                                                                      The killing of the Washington missionaries Marcus Whitman and his wife Narcissa, along with eleven others, on November 29, 1847 by members of the Cayuse tribe who accused Whitman of having poisoned 200 Cayuse in his medical care; launched the Cayuse War.

                                                                                                                                                                      Newsletter Articles

                                                                                                                                                                      There are currently no newsletter articles about Whitman Massacre (1847).
